width="auto"><div class="stMarkdown" data-testid="stMarkdown"><div data-testid="stMarkdownContainer" class="st-emotion-cache-1104ytp e1icttdg0"><p>UNIT ONE: MENTAL HEALTH AND PSYCHIATRIC NURSING</p>
<p>In this unit you will look at the basic concepts of mental health and illness, also covered is the process of admitting and discharging patients who are mentally ill. Additionally you will look at how mental health conditions are treated and managed, and community health services in the community.</p>
<p>This knowledge, and these skills and attitudes will help you to manage patients having psychosocial problems.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="this-unit-is-composed-of-five-sections">This unit is composed of five sections:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#this-unit-is-composed-of-five-sections" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Section One: Concepts, Principles and Theories of Mental Health and Psychiatric Nursing.
Section Two: Admission and Discharge Procedures of Mentally Sick Patients.
Section Three: Treatment Used in the Management of Mentally Ill Patients.
Section Four: Management of Common Mental Health Conditions.
Section Five: Community Mental Health.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="concepts-of-mental-health-and-mental-illness">Concepts of Mental Health and Mental Illness<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#concepts-of-mental-health-and-mental-illness" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="7368342c">What is meant by the term â€˜mental healthâ€™?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#7368342c" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Mental health is defined as the simultaneous success at working, loving, and creating with the capacity for mature and flexible resolution of conflicts between instincts, conscience, other people and reality (Evelyn and Wasili, 1986).</p>
<p>According to the World Health Organisation (WHO), mental health is a state of emotional well-being which enables one to function comfortably within society and to be satisfied with one's own achievements.</p>
<p>Mental health also refers to the ability of the individual to carry out their social role and to be able to adapt to their environment (Johnson, 1997).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="cfd50ff6">What do you understand by the term â€˜mental illnessâ€™?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cfd50ff6" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>A mental illness is defined as a disorder with psychological or behavioural manifestations and/or impairment of functioning due to a social, psychological, genetic, physical, chemical or biological disturbance (Evelyn and Wasili, 1986). A mentally ill person may have at least one of the following characteristics:</p>
<ul>
<li>Being dissatisfied with one's abilities and accomplishments</li>
<li>Having ineffective or unsatisfying interpersonal relationships</li>
<li>Dissatisfaction with one's place in the world</li>
<li>Having ineffective coping/adaptation mechanisms and lacking personal growth</li>
</ul>
<p>According to world health organization (WHO) mental health is a state of emotional well-being which enables one to function comfortably within society and to be satisfied with one's own achievements. True or False</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="theories-of-personality-development">Theories of Personality Development<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#theories-of-personality-development" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>For one said to be healthy, normal growth and development must have taken place. To assist in looking at</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>growth and development, you are going to look at the two main theories of personality development.</p>
<p>These are:</p>
<ul>
<li>Psychoanalytic theory by Sigmund Freud</li>
<li>Social learning theory by Erik Erickson</li>
</ul>
<p>You will now look at each of these theories in turn.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="psychoanalytic-theory">Psychoanalytic Theory<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#psychoanalytic-theory" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This theory will help you understand psychopathology and stress related behaviour. It will also help you explore human behaviour instead of taking behaviour at face value. The psychoanalytic theory makes several assumptions.</p>
<p>The theory posits that all human behaviour is determined by earlier life events and that human behaviour is driven by energy known as libido. It is also argued that people function at three levels</p>
<p>of awareness:</p>
<ul>
<li>Conscious level where immediate events and perceptions are stored</li>
<li>Pre-conscious level where thoughts and feelings are not accessible with ease</li>
<li>Unconscious level where material is not accessible most of the time</li>
</ul>
<p>According to the proponents of psychoanalysis, people develop through five stages:</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Stage</th><th>Age</th><th>Focus or Interests</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Oral</td><td>0 - 1</td><td>Focus on mouth, teeth and gums</td></tr><tr><td>Anal</td><td>1 - 3</td><td>Focus on control and self-control (primarily toilet training and defecation)</td></tr><tr><td>Phallic</td><td>3 - 6</td><td>Focus on genital stimulation and gender differentiation</td></tr><tr><td>Latency</td><td>7 - 11</td><td>Energy focused on non-sensual activity</td></tr><tr><td>Genital</td><td>12+</td><td>Development of mature sexual interests</td></tr></tbody></table>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="one-birth-to-1-year">One: Birth to 1 year<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#one-birth-to-1-year" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Oral phase, where sexual satisfaction is obtained through the mouth by actions of sucking or biting.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="two-1-year-to-3-years">Two: 1 year to 3 years<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#two-1-year-to-3-years" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Anal phase, where sexual satisfaction is obtained through the anus.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="three-3-years-to-6-years">Three: 3 years to 6 years<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#three-3-years-to-6-years" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Phallic phase, during which interest in the genitalia is developed and the individual acquires gender roles.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="four-7-years-to-11-years">Four: 7 years to 11 years<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#four-7-years-to-11-years" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Latent phase, where there is no sexual interest, this divides boys and girls into different groups.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="five-12-years-and-onwards">Five: 12 years and onwards<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#five-12-years-and-onwards" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Genital phase, when the capacity for objective and mature sex is developed.</p>
<p>According to this theory, the human personality is made up of three hypothetical structures:</p>
<p>Id: The id is the most primitive and is driven by impulses. It demands immediate gratification of the needs.</p>
<p>Super Ego: The super ego, whose main function is to oppose the id. It contains values, legal, moral regulations, and social expectations.</p>
<p>Ego: The ego, which unlike the id, is in contact with reality. It is able to delay the satisfaction of a need until an appropriate time, place, or object is available. It mediates between the id and the super ego.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260117-4ef26742.jpeg" alt="img-0.jpeg"></p>

Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers

Bishop's Computers</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="social-learning-theory">Social Learning Theory<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#social-learning-theory" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Erikson postulated eight human developmental stages which one has to go through in normal life. He called them psychosocial stages. Each stage is characterised by tasks or ego qualities, which one has to develop in normal life. You will now examine one stage at a time.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="trust-versus-mistrust">Trust versus Mistrust<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#trust-versus-mistrust" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This is attained during infancy. Trust is developed when the mother breastfeeds the infant as well as meeting other needs of the infant such as changing wet diapers. The approximate age at which the individual goes through this stage is 0 - 18 months.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="autonomy-versus-shame-and-doubt">Autonomy versus Shame and Doubt<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#autonomy-versus-shame-and-doubt" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>During this period the child wants some independence from the mother. This happens approximately at the age of 18 months to 3 years and this period is referred to as toddlerhood.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="initiative-versus-guilt">Initiative versus Guilt<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#initiative-versus-guilt" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This occurs at approximately 3 to 6 years, otherwise known as the pre-school years. The child is able to initiate action on its own in an effort to manipulate the environment.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="industry-versus-inferiority">Industry versus Inferiority<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#industry-versus-inferiority" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This takes place during school years between the ages of 6 to 12 years. The child is able to acquire skills in sports, calculate in figures and language skills are well developed.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="identity-versus-role-confusion">Identity versus Role Confusion<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#identity-versus-role-confusion" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This occurs around the age of 12 to 20 years and is referred to as adolescence. During this time an individual acquires an identity as a male or female corresponding to specific roles in the society.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="intimacy-versus-isolation">Intimacy versus Isolation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#intimacy-versus-isolation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This occurs at an approximate age of between 20 to 40 years. Here, one has productive work and has satisfactory sexual relations with an intimate member of the opposite sex.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="generativity-versus-stagnation">Generativity versus Stagnation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#generativity-versus-stagnation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This usually occurs between the ages of 45 to 65 years. During this period, one is involved in establishing and guiding the next generation. Productivity and creativity is at its peak.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="integrity-versus-despair">Integrity versus Despair<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#integrity-versus-despair" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This refers to the phase from around the age of 65 till death. During this time one develops new and different love for one's parents. One also develops emotional integration and is able to defend the dignity of one's own life-style against threat. The individual is capable of fellowship and will often take leadership responsibilities in the community.</p>
<p>It is worth noting that, it is only after satisfactory completion of one stage that one is ready to move to the next. Any person who is unable to go through one stage successfully would experience difficulties in subsequent stages of human development. For further details, please refer to psychology in module one.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="social-learning-theory">Social Learning Theory<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#social-learning-theory" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Using Erikson's theory, how would you counsel a couple whose only child has developmental problems during the adolescent period?</p>
<p>You should help the couple to assist their child to acquire acceptable social roles. You should also tell them how to guide their child to accept body changes and be able to socialise with age mates of both sexes. For more information, you can refer to your notes on the stage of identity versus role confusion.</p>
<p>Aetiological Factors of Mental Illness</p>
<p>You should now be familiar with the concepts of mental health.</p>
<p>You will now look at the components of psychiatric nursing, starting with the factors of mental illness.</p>
<p>The causes of mental illness can be classified into three categories:</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="predisposing-factors">Predisposing Factors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#predisposing-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>These factors determine the likelihood of one getting a mental illness. Usually they are adverse experiences one undergoes in early life. They include physical, psychological and social factors in infancy and early childhood.</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 6 of 185
Bishop's Computers</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="precipitating-factors">Precipitating Factors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#precipitating-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>These are events that take place shortly before the onset of a disorder. Physical precipitants include cerebral tumours, malaria or drug abuse. Social and psychological precipitants include misfortunes such as loss of a job, losing a loved person, or sudden change in routine activities.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="perpetuating-factors">Perpetuating Factors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#perpetuating-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Once the disorder has been triggered, these factors do prolong the course of the disease. They are secondary in nature since they may appear long after the original predisposing factors have been treated. Examples include secondary demoralisation and withdrawal from social activities.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="classification-of-mental-disorders">Classification of Mental Disorders<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#classification-of-mental-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>There are two major classifications of mental disorders used internationally.</p>
<p>These are:</p>
<ul>
<li>International Classification of Diseases (ICD)</li>
<li>Diagnostic and Statistical Manual (DSM)</li>
</ul>
<p>The ICD is the WHO system of classification, currently in its 10th edition, commonly referred to as ICD 10. The DSM classification is the American Psychiatric Association system, currently in the 4th edition and commonly referred to as DSM IV. For our learning purposes here, this module will use the WHO classification.</p>
<p>The rationale and other details relating to these classifications are beyond the scope of this module. Please find a copy and refer for details to the ICD 10 and DSM IV manuals, which are easily available in WHO and medical training college libraries.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="introducing-icd-10">Introducing ICD 10<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introducing-icd-10" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>ICD10 is classified in the following manner.</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>F0</th><th>Organic, including symptomatic mental disorders.</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>F1</td><td>Mental and behaviour disorders due to psychoactive substance use.</td></tr><tr><td>F2</td><td>Schizophrenia, schizotypal and delusional disorders.</td></tr><tr><td>F3</td><td>Mood (affective) disorders.</td></tr><tr><td>F4</td><td>Neurotic, stress related and somatoform disorders.</td></tr><tr><td>F5</td><td>Behavioural syndromes associated with physiological disturbances and physical factors.</td></tr><tr><td>F6</td><td>Disorders of adult personality and behaviour.</td></tr><tr><td>F7</td><td>Mental retardation.</td></tr><tr><td>F8</td><td>Disorders of psychological development.</td></tr><tr><td>F9</td><td>Behavioural and emotional disorders with onset usually occurring in childhood or adolescence.</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The main aims of the ICD 10 working party, when they drew up the classification system, were that they would create a system that:</p>
<ul>
<li>Was suitable for international communication on statistics of morbidity and mortality</li>
<li>Provides a reference for national and other psychiatric classifications</li>
<li>Is acceptable and useful in research and clinical work</li>
<li>Contributes to education</li>
</ul>
<p>To achieve these aims, the classification also had to be acceptable to a wide range of users in different cultures. It had to be practical in that it would be simple to use and easy to translate into</p>
<p>different languages.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="factors-that-influence-attitudes-towards-mental-health-and-mental-illness">Factors that Influence Attitudes towards Mental Health and Mental Illness<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#factors-that-influence-attitudes-towards-mental-health-and-mental-illness" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Having outlined the classification of mental illness, you will now turn your attention to the factors that influence attitudes towards mental health and mental illness. In this section, you are going to look at just a few examples.</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 7 of 185
Bishop's Computers</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="culture">Culture<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#culture" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The way people think, behave or feel is shaped by their culture. Culture also determines the features of insanity, for example, who is labelled as insane and under what circumstances.</p>
<p>What is considered insane in one culture may be considered perfectly normal in another. Culture also gives guidelines on the nature of treatment and the identity of the helper.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="education">Education<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#education" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The level of education also influences attitudes towards mental health and mental illness.</p>
<p>An educated person has a better understanding of health and mental illness, thus making their attitude more positive.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="health-beliefs">Health Beliefs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#health-beliefs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>These will determine whether the individual's attitude is positive or negative. It will depend on how the patient explains the illness to themselves, that is, whether they believe in germ theory, evil spirits or an imbalance of some kind.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="religion">Religion<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#religion" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A patient's reaction to mental illness will often depend on whether or not the patient believes in God or a particular religion, for example, some religions believe that ill health is caused by evil spirits. Usually, religion encourages the followers to be empathetic to sick people.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="principles-and-qualities-of-psychiatric-nursing">Principles and Qualities of Psychiatric Nursing<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#principles-and-qualities-of-psychiatric-nursing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Having looked at the factors that influence attitudes towards mental health and mental illness, you will now look at the principles of psychiatric nursing and various ways of assisting the patient to overcome the prevailing problems.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="respect-for-the-patient">Respect for the Patient<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#respect-for-the-patient" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is achieved by accepting the patient as they are.</p>
<p>The therapist should take time to listen to the patient and provide privacy for all conversations. Minimise situations and experiences that might humiliate the patient and be honest in providing information on medicines, privileges, length of management and stays in hospital if indicated.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="availability">Availability<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#availability" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The nurse must be constantly available to assist the patient to attain their basic needs and alleviate suffering.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="spontaneity">Spontaneity<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#spontaneity" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>You should avoid being overly formal. Instead, you should be comfortable with yourself, be flexible and aware of the therapeutic goals.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="acceptance">Acceptance<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#acceptance" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Even if the patient behaves in a way that does not please the nurse, they should be accepted as they are, but taking care not to reinforce their behaviour.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="sensitivity">Sensitivity<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sensitivity" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>You should do your best to show genuine interest and concern.</p>
<p>You should be persistent and patient even if no observable improvement is made.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="accountability">Accountability<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#accountability" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Since mentally ill patients are vulnerable due to their distorted thinking and behaviour, accountability is required more in a psychiatric setting than any other type of health care (Peplau, cited by Wilson and Kneisl, 1988). You are also accountable to yourself as well as professional colleagues and peers.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="empathy">Empathy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#empathy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is the process of putting yourself in another's shoes and remaining emotionally detached. The nurse should strive to understand the patient's perspective, and work toward mutually developed goals.</p>
<p>The most important function of empathy is that it enables you to give the patient the feeling of being understood and cared about.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="self-understanding">Self-understanding<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#self-understanding" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This involves recognition and acceptance of your own behaviour and how it affects your relationship with other people.</p>
<p>This will inevitably help you, as a therapist, to understand other peoples' behaviour, needs and problems.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="permissiveness-and-firmness">Permissiveness and Firmness<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#permissiveness-and-firmness" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Although you have been told to accept the patient as they are, this does not mean that you are in a position to allow them to do whatever they like. The therapist is expected to set limits and to be firm in implementing them.</p>
<p>Skill in Observation</p>
<p>It is important for a psychiatric nurse to be alert and observant at all times of the patient's behaviour, attitudes and how they react to staff, relatives and fellow patients.</p>
<p>Historical Trends in Psychiatric Nursing</p>
<p>Psychiatric nursing, and the understanding of mental illness, with which it associates, has developed in several epochs through the centuries. You will now look at each of those epochs in more detail.</p>
<p>Demonological Period</p>
<p>The earliest records of a person believed to have suffered from mental illness relate to king Nebuchadnezzar, who ate grass believing that he was an ox. Another example is Ajax, who impaled himself on a sword believing that he was tormented by demons.</p>
<p>During that time people believed that the cause of mental illness was demons. The treatment was quite harsh, degrading and dehumanising and involved beating, chaining, locking the individual up in a dark room and throwing the individual into rivers and ponds.</p>
<p>Those patients who escaped this harsh treatment survived on stealing food or eating wild fruits. Wild animals ate up those who inadvertently wandered into the forest.</p>
<p>Political Period</p>
<p>This period is associated with King Edward II of England.</p>
<p>During that time, a law was passed in the parliament to protect the property of the mentally sick. In the year 1403, the Sisters of the Order of Saint Mary managed to start a facility to care for the mentally sick at Bedlam. The facility was able to accommodate six patients only. Thereafter, other hospitals followed the example.</p>
<p>The cause of mental illness, however, was still thought to be demons. The treatment, therefore, remained more or less as in the demonological period. Facilities were often dark, humid and infested with lice. They were also overcrowded, leading to mass deaths during outbreaks of disease such as the plague.</p>
<p>In the early 18th century, the first qualified nurse was appointed to look after the mentally ill by Edward Tyson. However, although qualified, the nurses appointed to look after the mentally sick were equally harsh to patients.</p>
<p>Men and women were housed together and members of the public used to visit these facilities as a form of entertainment. It was at St. Luke's hospital in London where this form of entertainment was eventually banned. In order to enforce the policy, members of the public were only allowed to see the mentally ill in the presence of an attendant after being issued with a ticket.</p>
<p>Humanitarian Period</p>
<p>During this period, reforms of the patient care system for the mentally ill began in France, followed by Britain and later America.</p>
<p>Reform in France started in 1793 at Bicetre Hospital in Paris.</p>
<p>Dr. Philippe Pinel unchained a group of patients who had been in chains for 30 years. He advocated kindness for mentally sick persons, and as a result there was a marked improvement in mentally sick patients.</p>
<p>William Tuke started reforms in Britain in 1796. He advocated humane treatment of the mentally sick. In addition, he introduced what we today call 'occupational therapy'. Men were involved in gardening while women were involved in sewing. Both men and women assisted attendants in their daily work activities. It is worth noting that so far, members of staff were not specifically trained to deal with mental health issues. In 1808, a bill was passed to regulate the treatment of mental health patients.</p>
<p>In America, Dorothea Lynda Dix introduced reforms after visiting Britain and seeing how mentally sick persons were improving after getting reformed type of management. In 1841, she managed to have a bill passed in parliament to regulate the treatment of the mentally sick in America.</p>
<p>In 1853, Dr. W.A.F Browne started giving informal mental health lectures to nurses so as to give quality care.</p>
<p>By 1882, formal training on mental health had begun in America at McLean Hospital, Boston.</p>
<p>In 1884, formal training in mental health was started in Germany and thereafter other countries followed that example.</p>
<p>The Scientific Period</p>
<p>The scientific period is associated with the 19th Century. During that period science was devoted to developing modern treatments that were based on scientific findings. Many forms of treatments were discovered and later abandoned like hydrotherapy, insulin therapy and leucotomy.</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>The current forms of treatments include physical treatment like chemotherapy and electroconvulsive therapy.</p>
<p>There are also various psychological treatments, which include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Individual/group psychotherapy</li>
<li>Behaviour therapy</li>
<li>Occupational therapy</li>
<li>Rehabilitation</li>
<li>Cognitive therapy</li>
<li>Counselling</li>
</ul>
<p>Some of these treatments will be covered in more detail in section two of this unit</p>
<p>The scientific period witnessed the integration of mental health services with other health services. Trained manpower was developed to care for the mentally sick.</p>
<p>Men and women were either managed separately or in the same wards, depending on the policy of the particular hospital.</p>
<p>Children were managed in special wards. Where resources were available, different mental health conditions were managed in different units</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="development-of-psychiatry-and-mental-health-services-in-kenya">Development of Psychiatry and Mental Health Services in Kenya<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#development-of-psychiatry-and-mental-health-services-in-kenya" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The current Mathari hospital was started in July 1910 as a lunatic asylum. Before then, the facility served as a smallpox isolation centre. The asylum was renamed Mathari Mental Hospital in 1924. The care was mainly custodial, taking place in dark, gloomy and often damp conditions.</p>
<p>Europeans, Africans, and Asians were managed separately and the quality of mental health care provided depended on the individual's racial background.</p>
<p>Mathari was the only mental hospital until the 1962 Decentralisation of Mental Health Services Act. Other facilities began to spring up, including a 22 bed psychiatric unit in Nakuru in 1962, Machakos in 1963, Nyeri and Muranga in 1964 and Port Reitz and Kakamega in 1965.</p>
<p>Currently all provincial hospitals have operational psychiatric units. However, only some district hospitals have operational psychiatric units. Outpatient psychiatric clinics have been established in most of the district hospitals.</p>
<p>Mathari hospital is being redeveloped, and the future plan is to intensify community based psychiatric services all over the country. It is worth noting that community psychiatric services were established in Nairobi in 1983.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="training-of-mental-health-workers">Training of Mental Health Workers<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#training-of-mental-health-workers" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The training of enrolled psychiatric nurses was started in 1961 and later changed to a post enrolled psychiatric nursing course. In 1963, the first two registered psychiatric nurses were trained overseas.</p>
<p>In 1979, a post basic diploma in psychiatric nursing was started in Kenya. Between 1972 and 1982 most psychiatrists received overseas training at the Institute of Psychiatry in England.</p>
<p>In 1982, the University of Nairobi started training psychiatrists.</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>SECTION 2: ADMISSION AND DISCHARGE PROCEDURES OF MENTALLY SICK PATIENTS</p>
<p>Introduction</p>
<p>In this section, you will need to use the knowledge you gained on the classification of mental disorders.</p>
<p>You will look closely at the admission and discharge procedure of mentally sick persons using the Mental Health Act.</p>
<p>Objectives</p>
<p>At the end of this section you will be able to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Apply the knowledge acquired on legal aspects in admission and discharge of patients</li>
<li>Demonstrate skills in history taking</li>
</ul>
<p>Mental Health Act (Cap 248) and Legal Application</p>
<p>The Mental Health Act is an act of parliament to amend and consolidate the law relating to the care of persons who are suffering from mental disorders, or mental sub-normality with mental disorder, for the custody of these persons, management of their properties, management and control of a mental hospital and for custodial purposes.</p>
<p>The act provides for the procedures to be followed for reception into a mental hospital. It also stipulates that no person shall be received or detained for treatment in a mental hospital, unless they have been received and detained under this act or under criminal procedure code.</p>
<p>Kenyan Board of Mental Health</p>
<p>The act also provides for the establishment of a board, that is, the Kenya board of mental health for</p>
<p>the purposes of administering this act.</p>
<p>The members of the Kenya board of mental health include:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Chairman, who can be the Director of Medical Services (DMS) or the Deputy Director of Medical Services and is appointed by the minister.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Psychiatrist (medical practitioner) appointed by the minister.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>One clinical officer with training and experience in mental health care appointed by the minister.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>One psychiatric nurse with experience in mental health care, appointed by the minister.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The commissioner of social services or their nominee appointed by the minister.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Director of education or their nominee appointed by the minister.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A representative from each province in Kenya, being resident in the provinces, appointed by the minister.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>The board may co-opt any person whose skills, knowledge or experience may be useful. It may also establish a committee for better function and regulate its own procedure.</p>
<p>The functions of the Board are under the control and direction of the minister for health.</p>
<p>They include:</p>
<ul>
<li>To coordinate mental health activities in Kenya.</li>
<li>To advise the government on the state of mental health and mental health care facilities in Kenya.</li>
<li>To inspect mental health care hospitals to ensure that they meet the prescribed standards.</li>
<li>To approve the establishment of mental health care hospitals.</li>
<li>To assist when necessary in the administration of mental health hospitals.</li>
<li>To receive and investigate any matters referred to it by a patient or relative of a patient concerning the treatment of the patient at a mental health hospital and, where necessary, to take or recommend to the minister any remedial action.</li>
<li>To advise the government on the care of the persons suffering from mental sub-normality without mental disorder.</li>
<li>To initiate and organise community or family based programmes for the care of persons suffering from mental disorder, and to perform such other functions as may be placed upon it by this act or under the law.</li>
</ul>
<p>Sections of the Mental Health Act</p>
<p>Part V - Voluntary Patients (Section 10)</p>
<p>Any person who has attained the apparent age of sixteen years, decrees to voluntarily submit themselves to treatment for mental disorder, and who makes to the 'person in charge' a written</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>application in duplicate in the form prescribed, may be perceived as a voluntary patient into a mental hospital.</p>
<p>The person fills in a form MOH 613, in duplicate provided for in the first schedule to these regulations before admitting them to the institution as an in-patient. This indicates that the admission is at their own request.</p>
<p>Any person who has not attained the apparent age of sixteen years and whose parent or guardian desires to submit them for treatment for mental disorder, may if the guardian or parent makes to the 'person in charge' of a mental institution, a written application in duplicate in the prescribed forms, be perceived as a voluntary patient. In such cases forms MOH 637 in duplicate should be filled and signed by the guardian or the parent.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="part-vi-involuntary-patients-section-14-m-h-a">Part VI - Involuntary Patients (Section 14 M.H.A)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#part-vi-involuntary-patients-section-14-m-h-a" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Involuntary patients are those who are incapable of expressing themselves as willing or unwilling to receive treatment. They require the forms MOH 614 to be filled in duplicate by the husband, wife or relative of the patient, indicating the reasons why they are applying for admission.</p>
<p>Any person applying on behalf of another person should state the reasons why a relative could not make the application and specify their connection with the patient.</p>
<p>The patient is admitted for a period of not more than six months. The 'person in charge' can prolong this period by six more months provided the total period does not exceed twelve months. An MOH 615 form should be filled by the doctor indicating why he thinks that the patient can benefit from the treatment. They should write down their own name, qualifications, date and then sign the forms.</p>
<p>Both the MOH 614 and MOH 615 forms must reach the hospital within 14 days of the date they were signed, otherwise they become invalid.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="part-vii-emergency-admissions-section-1b-m-h-a">Part VII - Emergency Admissions (Section 1b M.H.A)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#part-vii-emergency-admissions-section-1b-m-h-a" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A police officer, chief or assistant chief can arrest any person who is found to be dangerous to themselves or others, and take them to a mental hospital for treatment within 24 hours or a reasonable time. The patient should be reviewed after 72 hours and can be discharged if found to be of sound mind. If found to be of unsound mind, the patient may be admitted for treatment as an involuntary patient. For the purposes of admission, the form MOH 638 must be filled in by the police officer or an administrative officer.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="part-viii-admission-and-discharge-of-members-of-the-armed-forces-section-17-m-h-a">Part VIII - Admission and Discharge of Members of the Armed Forces (Section 17 M.H.A)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#part-viii-admission-and-discharge-of-members-of-the-armed-forces-section-17-m-h-a" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Any member of the armed forces may be admitted into a mental hospital for observation, if a medical officer of the armed forces, by letter addressed to the 'person in charge', and certifies that:</p>
<ul>
<li>The member of the armed forces has been examined within a period of 48 hours before issuing the letter</li>
<li>For reasons recorded in the letter, the member of the armed forces is a proper person to be admitted to a mental hospital for observation and treatment</li>
</ul>
<p>A member of the armed forces may be admitted under section 17 for an initial period of 28 days from the date of admission, that period may be extended if, at or before the end of 28 days, two medical practitioners, one of whom shall be a psychiatrist, recommend the extension after re-examining the patient.</p>
<p>The said patient can be discharged if two medical practitioners, one of whom is a psychiatrist, by a letter addressed to the 'person in charge', certifying that they have examined the member of the armed forces within a period of 72 hours before issuing the letter.</p>
<p>Where any member of the armed forces suffers from mental illness whilst away from his armed forces unit and is under any circumstance, admitted into a mental hospital, the 'person in charge' shall inform the nearest armed forces unit directly, or through an administrative officer or gazetted police officer.</p>
<p>If a member of the armed forces is admitted to a mental hospital they cease to be a member of the armed forces, the 'person in charge' shall be informed of that fact and the patient shall be declared an involuntary patient under part VI (section 14) with effect from the date the information is received.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="part-ix-admission-of-a-patient-from-foreign-countries-section-18-m-h-a">Part IX - Admission of a Patient from Foreign Countries (Section 18 M.H.A)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#part-ix-admission-of-a-patient-from-foreign-countries-section-18-m-h-a" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>According to this section of the act:</p>
<ul>
<li>No person suffering from mental disorder shall be admitted into a mental hospital in Kenya from any state outside Kenya except under Part IX of M.H.A.</li>
<li>This part will not apply to individuals ordinarily resident in Kenya.</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>(Section 19 M.H.A) Where it is necessary to admit a person suffering from mental disorder from any foreign country into any mental hospital in Kenya for observation, the government or other relevant authority in that country shall apply in writing to the mental health board to approve the admission, no mental hospital shall receive a person suffering mental disorders from a foreign country without the board's written approval.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The application for the board's approval under subsection (I) shall indicate that the person whom it relates to has been legally detained in the foreign country for a period not exceeding two months under the law in that country, relating to the detention and treatment of persons suffering from mental disorder, and their admission into mental hospital in Kenya has been found necessary.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>No person shall be admitted under this section unless they are accompanied by a warrant or other documents together with the board's approval under subsection (2) shall be sufficient authority for their conveyance to admission and treatment in the mental hospital to which the board's approval relates.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>According to this section of the act:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>On the admission of a person into a mental hospital under this section, not being a person transferred to the mental hospital under section 23, the 'person in charge' shall within 72 hours or such longer period as the board may approve (i) Examine the person or cause the person to be examined to determine the extent of the mental disorder and the nature of treatment and (ii) Within that period forward to the Board a report on the findings, together with the warrant or other document from the foreign country concerned accompanying the patient/person.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A person shall not be detained in a mental hospital under this section for a period longer than two months from the date of admission to the mental hospital unless the board, on application in the prescribed forms by the 'person in charge', approves.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="c180e939">Part X â€“ Discharge and Transfer of Patients (Section 21 and 22 of M.H.A)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#c180e939" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The 'person in charge' of a mental hospital may, by order in writing, and upon the recommendation of the medical practitioner in charge of any person's treatment in the mental hospital, recommend discharge and that person shall thereupon be discharged as having recovered from mental disorder, provided that:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>An order shall not be made under this section for a person who is detained under criminal procedure Cap 75.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>This section shall not prejudice the board's powers under section 15 of M.H.A.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="section-15-provides-that">Section 15 provides that:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#section-15-provides-that" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Where any person has been received into a mental hospital under part V and part VI (voluntary and involuntary mode of admission), the board may at any time order that the person shall be discharged or otherwise dealt with under this act.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="section-22-order-for-delivery-of-patient-into-care-of-relative-of-friend">Section 22: Order for delivery of patient into care of relative of friend.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#section-22-order-for-delivery-of-patient-into-care-of-relative-of-friend" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>If any relative or friend of a person admitted into any mental hospital under this act desires to take the person into their custody and care, they may apply to the 'person in charge' who may, subject to subsection (2), order that the person be delivered into the custody and care of the relative or friend upon such terms and conditions to be complied with by the relative or friend.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>In the exercise of their powers subsection (1) the person in charge shall consult with the medical practitioner in charge of the person's treatment in the mental hospital and the board on the relevant district mental health council, which is performing the board's functions under section 7, subsection (1).</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="15032c4f">Part XIV â€“ Offences under MHA<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#15032c4f" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="section-47">Section 47:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#section-47" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It is an offence for a person other than medical practitioner to sign certificates.</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 13 of 185
Bishop's Computers</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="section-48">Section 48:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#section-48" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Any medical practitioner who knowingly, wilfully or recklessly certifies anything in a certificate made under this act, which they know to be untrue, shall be guilty of an offence.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="section-49">Section 49:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#section-49" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It is an offence for any person to assist the escape of any person suffering from mental disorder being conveyed to or from, or while under care and treatment in a mental hospital. It is also an offence to harbour any person suffering from mental disorder that they know have escaped from a mental hospital.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="section-50">Section 50:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#section-50" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It is an offence for any person in charge of or any person employed at a mental hospital to unlawfully permit a patient to leave such a hospital.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="section-51">Section 51:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#section-51" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Any person in charge of, or any person employed at a mental hospital that strikes, ill-treats, abuses or wilfully neglects any patient in the mental hospital, shall be guilty of an offence.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="section-52">Section 52:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#section-52" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Any person who without the consent of a 'person in charge' gives, sells or barters any articles or commodities of any kind, to any patient in a mental hospital, whether inside or outside the grounds of the mental hospital, shall be guilty of an offence.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="section-53">Section 53:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#section-53" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>General Penalty: Any person who is guilty of an offence under this act, or who contravenes any of the provisions of this act or any regulations made under this act, shall where no other penalty is provided, be liable on conviction to a fine not exceeding Ksh 10,000. or to imprisonment not exceeding twelve months or both.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="history-taking">History Taking<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#history-taking" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>History taking from a mentally ill person or their relatives will assist you to make a nursing diagnosis and to give holistic care to the patient. You are now going to look at all the steps involved in history taking.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="personal-data">Personal Data<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#personal-data" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Here you ask for information pertaining to age, sex, marital status, occupation, residence and nationality.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="personal-history">Personal History<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#personal-history" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Ask the patient questions relating to their mode of delivery, as well as milestones in infancy and early childhood.</p>
<p>You may ask the patient when they started school and their educational performance as well as about possible incidents of traumatic experience like falling or losing a parent.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="social-history">Social History<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#social-history" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>You should try to find out about the nature of the patient's occupation, how they relate to both sexes, whether they are outgoing or not, the number of friends the patient has of both sexes and whether or not the patient is involved in religious activities.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="sexual-history">Sexual History<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sexual-history" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In taking down this information, you are aiming to check the degree of sexual satisfaction with the marriage partner, male or female friend, frequency of sexual relationships and the patient's attitude to sex.</p>
