<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="family-history">Family History<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#family-history" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Ask the patient about their parents, brothers and sisters. For each one of them you are trying to find out whether they are married, occupation etc.</p>
<p>in an attempt to identify possible family behavioural patterns.</p>
<p>If the patient is married, try and find out the sibling line up of the patient's spouse as well.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="past-medical-and-psychiatric-history">Past Medical and Psychiatric History<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#past-medical-and-psychiatric-history" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>By taking down the patient's medical history, you are in a position to find out about any medical conditions the patient has suffered, which may have affected their mental health.</p>
<p>You should also try and find out if there have been any incidences of the patient being</p>
<p>admitted into a mental unit/hospital and the outcome of the treatment.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="history-of-presenting-illness">History of Presenting Illness<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#history-of-presenting-illness" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Ask the patient about the onset of the illness, duration, any allegations that brought them to the mental hospital and the patient's pre-morbid history, that is, how they presented before they became mentally ill.</p>
<p><strong>Remember:</strong></p>
<p>In an outpatient clinic, this information is better taken first, since the patient or the informant would like to talk about it straight away.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="mental-status-assessment">Mental Status Assessment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mental-status-assessment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Check facial expressions to provide information about mood, orientation to time, place, person, concentration and perceptual disorder, where you should check for the following senses:</p>
<ul>
<li>Olfactory</li>
<li>Auditory</li>
<li>Tactile</li>
<li>Visual</li>
<li>Gustatory</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="thought-content">Thought Content<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#thought-content" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>When checking the thought content, you should be on the lookout for grandiose or persecutory delusions, delusions of worthlessness or of preference and thought insertion and thought broadcasting.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="memory">Memory<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#memory" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Pay attention to immediate memory (min/hrs), recent memory (days, weeks, months) and past or remote memory (10 years and above).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="mood">Mood<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mood" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Try and evaluate whether the patient is manic, depressed, labile or flat.</p>
<p>You should also try and establish the patient's judgment, by checking for signs of logical thinking. In addition, you should look into whether or not the patient has 'insight', that is, whether or not they are aware of their mental illness.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="physical-examination">Physical Examination<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#physical-examination" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Conduct a general examination, checking for scars, deformity and number of teeth not in place.</p>
<p>Also check vital signs of temperature, pulse, respiration and blood pressure.</p>
<p>After conducting all these checks you should be able to make a provisional nursing diagnosis and draw up a plan of care using the nursing process.</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 15 of 185
Bishop's Computers</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="section-3-treatment-used-in-the-management-of-mentally-ill-persons">SECTION 3: TREATMENT USED IN THE MANAGEMENT OF MENTALLY ILL PERSONS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#section-3-treatment-used-in-the-management-of-mentally-ill-persons" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="introduction">Introduction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In this section you will look at indications, effects, side effects and contraindications of various drugs used in the management of mentally ill patients. These drugs fall under the categories of tranquilisers, antidepressants, anti-anxiety and antiparkinsonian drugs.</p>
<p>Also you will cover psychological treatment, psychotherapy, behaviour therapy and rehabilitation.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="objectives">Objectives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>At the end of this section you will be able to describe treatments under the following headings:</p>
<ul>
<li>Drugs and other physical treatments</li>
<li>Psychological treatments</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="drugs-and-other-physical-treatments">Drugs and Other Physical Treatments<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#drugs-and-other-physical-treatments" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>There are various types of drugs and other physical treatments used to treat patients suffering from mental health illness.</p>
<p>These can be grouped together under the following categories:</p>
<ul>
<li>Antipsychotic Medication</li>
<li>Antidepressant</li>
<li>Anxiolytics or Anti-anxiety Drugs</li>
<li>Antiparkinsonian Drugs</li>
<li>Electroconvulsive Therapy (ECT)</li>
</ul>
<p>You will now look at each of these categories in turn.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="antipsychotic-medication">Antipsychotic Medication<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#antipsychotic-medication" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Antipsychotic drugs are also called major tranquilisers or neuroleptics used in the treatment of psychoses like schizophrenia, bipolar disorders (manic phase) and alcohol withdrawal disorder.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="antipsychotic-drugs">Antipsychotic Drugs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#antipsychotic-drugs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<table><thead><tr><th>Generic Name</th><th>Trade Name</th><th>Daily Doses (range)</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Low Potency Drugs</td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Chlorpromazine</td><td>Largactil</td><td>300-1000mgs</td></tr><tr><td>Sulpride</td><td>Domatil,Sulparex</td><td>200-2400mg</td></tr><tr><td>Thioridazine</td><td>Melleril</td><td>50-800mg</td></tr><tr><td>High Potency Drugs</td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Haloperidol</td><td>Haldol,Serenace</td><td>1-20mg</td></tr><tr><td>Thiothixene</td><td>Navane</td><td>6-60mgs</td></tr><tr><td>Zoxapine</td><td>Loxitane</td><td>60-250mgs</td></tr><tr><td>Molindone</td><td>Lidone</td><td>50-400mgs</td></tr><tr><td>Flupenthixol</td><td>Depixol</td><td>6-18mg</td></tr><tr><td>Fluphenazine</td><td>Moditen</td><td>2.5-20mg</td></tr><tr><td>Trifluoperazine</td><td>Stelazine</td><td>5-30mg</td></tr><tr><td>Zuclopenthixol</td><td>Clopixol</td><td>20-150mg</td></tr><tr><td>Pimozide</td><td>Orap</td><td>2-10mg</td></tr><tr><td>Depot Injections</td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Fluphenazine decanoate</td><td>Modecate</td><td>12.5-100mg(IM 2 Weekly)</td></tr><tr><td>Zuclopenthixol Acetate</td><td>Clopixol Acuphase</td><td>50-150mg every 2-3 days</td></tr><tr><td>Haloperidol decanoate</td><td>Haldol decanoate</td><td>50-300mg (IM 4 weekly)</td></tr></tbody></table>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="mechanisms-of-action">Mechanisms of Action<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mechanisms-of-action" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The drugs are thought to work by blocking dopamine receptors causing a decrease in psychotic symptoms. The drug is metabolised in the liver and excreted by the kidneys. For one to get the desired effects, one must maintain the patient on the lowest dose possible and initial therapy should be on divided doses so that the patient can be monitored.</p>
<p>For acutely psychotic patients:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Give intramuscular haloperidol, for example, 5mg every 30 to 60 minutes over a two to six hour period. Peak level is attained 20 to 40 minutes after injection.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Monitor blood pressure before each dose and withhold if the systolic blood pressure is 90mm Hg or below.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Sleep state should be monitored to ensure six to seven hours of sleep.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Dystonia occurring 1 hour to 48 hours after starting treatment should be treated with an antiparkinsonism drug.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>To decrease the danger to the patient themselves and others, the patient needs to be monitored for possible adverse reactions to the medication.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Drugs should be given using the following time frame:</p>
<ul>
<li>Six months for first psychotic episode.</li>
<li>One year period for second psychotic episode.</li>
<li>Indefinite period for third and later psychotic episodes.</li>
</ul>
<p>The drug should be discontinued through tapering the dosage to avoid dyskinesia.</p>
<p>Gertrude and MacFarland (1986) have identified the following expected responses to the treatment:</p>
<ul>
<li>Initially the patient is drowsy and cooperative within hours to a week.</li>
<li>The patient becomes more sociable and less withdrawn for the next two months.</li>
<li>The thought disorder generally disappears in six weeks or more.</li>
<li>Improvement is generally noted in hallucinations, acute delusions, sleeping habits, appetite, tension, combativeness, hostility, negativism and personal grooming.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Remember:</strong>
Use of more than one phenothiazine is not recommended.
Geriatric patients should be given lower dosages to avoid hypertension due to prolonged half-life in people aged over 55 years.</p>
<p><strong>Side Effects</strong>
There are several side effects that may be experienced by patients. These include drowsiness and orthostatic hypotension, especially after im injections. The patient may also experience extra pyramidal symptoms like:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Dystonia, that is, spasms of muscles of face, neck, back, eye, arms and legs.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Oculogyric crisis, presenting as fixed upward gaze from spasm of oculomotor muscles.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Torticollis, that is, pulling of the head to the side from spasm of cervical muscles.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Opisthotonus, which refers to the hyperextension of the back from spasm of back muscles.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Akathisia or continuous motor restlessness.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Akinesia or lack of body movement especially arms.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Pseudoparkinsonism, which presents with a shuffling gait, mask-like facial expression, tremor, rigidity and akinesia.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>The patient may also experience tardive dyskinesia, that is, a wormlike movement of the tongue, frequent blinking, and involuntary movement of tongue, lips and jaw. They may experience convulsive seizures or allergic or toxic effects (some of which are rare and serious).</p>
<p>These include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Aggranulosis</li>
<li>Oral monoliasis</li>
<li>Dermatitis</li>
<li>Jaundice</li>
</ul>
<p>The patient may also exhibit other side effects including endocrine or metabolic effects like weight gain or decreased libido, impotence, impaired ejaculation in males. They may also have decreased thermoregulatory ability and as a result might complain of being too cold or too hot.</p>
<p>Adjusting the dosage of antipsychotic drugs, and giving antiparkinsonian drugs can often be quite effective in treating side effects.</p>
<p><strong>Contraindications</strong>
Comatose, glaucoma, prosthetic hyperplastic, acute myocardial infarction are contraindications to the use of these drugs (Gertrude and McFarland, 1986).</p>
<p><strong>Antidepressants</strong>
These drugs are used to treat affective disorders.</p>
<p><strong>Mechanisms of Action</strong>
They act by increasing epinephrine and serotonin. Both of them are metabolised in the liver and excreted in the urine.</p>
<p>Table showing some examples of antidepressant drugs.</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Major Groups</th><th>Generic Name</th><th>Trade Name</th><th>Daily Dosage (range)</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Tricyclic antidepressants</td><td>Amitriptyline</td><td>Elavil (laroxyl)</td><td>75-300mg</td></tr><tr><td></td><td>Imipramine</td><td>Tofranil</td><td>100-300mg</td></tr><tr><td>Tetra cyclic anti-depressants</td><td>Maprotiline</td><td>Ludiomi I</td><td>75-300mg</td></tr><tr><td>Monoamine Oxidase Inhibitors</td><td>Isocarboxacid</td><td>Marplan</td><td>10-60mg</td></tr><tr><td></td><td>Phenelzine</td><td>Nardil</td><td>45-90mg</td></tr><tr><td>Selective Serotonin Reuptake Inhibitors</td><td>Fluoxetine</td><td>Prozac</td><td>20mg</td></tr><tr><td></td><td>Citalopram</td><td>Ciprami I</td><td>20-60mg</td></tr><tr><td></td><td>Paroxetine</td><td>Seroxat</td><td>10-50mg</td></tr></tbody></table>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="mechanisms-of-action">Mechanisms of Action<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mechanisms-of-action" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>For the drugs to be effective:</p>
<ul>
<li>Dosage may be divided, but the total dose can be given at bed time due to the sedative effects.</li>
<li>Minimum dose should be given then increased gradually.</li>
<li>5 to 21 days must be allowed before any mood change is observed.</li>
<li>four to six weeks must be allowed to pass for therapeutic effects to be observed.</li>
<li>Medication needs to be continued for 6 months after patient is free from depression.</li>
</ul>
<p>The patient may respond to the treatment in several ways.</p>
<p>They may exhibit drowsiness in early stages, which later subsides. Hypotension may be experienced initially, leading to feeling of fainting. Withdrawal symptoms may be experienced if the drug is not gradually stopped.</p>
<p>As previously mentioned, lower dosages are indicated for geriatric patients since they are more sensitive to the drug and its side effects.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="side-effects">Side Effects<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#side-effects" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>According to Gertrude and McFarland (1986), some of the side effects that might be experienced include mild anticholinergic effects from tricyclic and monoamine oxidase inhibitors, dry mouth, constipation, blurred vision, tachycardia nausea, oedema, hypotension and urinary retention. Adjusting the dosage to a lower level will usually resolve the problem.</p>
<p>Side effects that are specific to tricyclics are:</p>
<ul>
<li>Allergic reactions manifested as skin rash and jaundice.</li>
<li>Tachycardia.</li>
<li>Tremors.</li>
<li>Long term treatment may depress bone marrow, predispose to sore throat and aching, and fever.</li>
</ul>
<p>Under such circumstances, stopping the use of the drug is the intervention of choice.</p>
<p>Meanwhile, specific side effects of monoamine oxidase inhibitors include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Liver damage that is rare but fatal.</li>
<li>Precipitation of manic episodes.</li>
<li>Hypertension crisis characterised by severe headache palpitation, neck stiffness, nausea, vomiting, increased Bp, chest pain and collapse. It occurs 30 minutes to 24 hours after eating food containing tyramine. These foods include cheese, wine, beer, sour cream, liver, chocolate, bananas, avocados, soy sauce, and beans.</li>
</ul>
<p>The main form of treatment when side effects occur is to discontinue the drug and then give regitine to lower the blood pressure.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="contraindications">Contraindications<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#contraindications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The use of antidepressants is contraindicated when the patient suffers from glaucoma, agitated states, urinary retention, cardiac disorders and seizure disorders.</p>
<p>Having looked at major tranquilisers and antidepressants, now you will look at minor tranquilisers.</p>
<p><strong>Remember:</strong></p>
<p>Anti-depressants should be discontinued prior to surgery.</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 18 of 185
Bishop's Computers</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="anxiolytics-or-anti-anxiety-drugs">Anxiolytics or Anti-anxiety Drugs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#anxiolytics-or-anti-anxiety-drugs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>These drugs, when given to a patient having generalised anxiety disorder, are able to provide relief.</p>
<p>They are mainly recommended for acute anxiety states, which may present with palpitations, sweating, trembling, shortness of breath, chest pain, nausea, dizziness, a feeling of unreality, fear of losing control or dying, chills or numbness.</p>
<p>Examples of these drugs include buspirone, a novel anxiolytic, and benzodiazepines like diazepam and lorazepam.</p>
<p>For the purposes of your study, you are mainly interested in diazepines.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="effects">Effects<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#effects" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The main effects include sedation, muscle relaxation and elevation of seizure threshold.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="side-effects">Side Effects<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#side-effects" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Side effects include dizziness, headache, nervousness, insomnia, light headedness, dry mouth, nausea, vomiting, abdominal and gastric distress and diarrhoea.</p>
<p>When high doses of medication are used for more than four months, the patient is likely to develop drug dependence or withdrawal syndrome.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="contraindications">Contraindications<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#contraindications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Benzodiazepines should not be used together with other central nervous system depressants. They should be given with caution to patients who are elderly, depressed or suicidal and those with a history of substance abuse.</p>
<p>It is worth noting that these drugs need to be combined with psychotherapy to ensure complete cure of the problem.</p>
<p>This implies that anxiolytics by themselves are not a cure for psychological problems. The most commonly used drug is diazepam. This is usually administered as a dose of 2-10mg bid/qid orally or 2-20mg i.m. or i.v. This can be repeated one hour after the initial dose.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="antiparkinsonian-drugs">Antiparkinsonian Drugs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#antiparkinsonian-drugs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>These are drugs given to counteract the side effects of major tranquilisers.</p>
<p>An example of such a drug is benztropine (cogentin) whose initial dose is 0.1-1mg daily, the maintenance dose is 0.5-6mg daily divided into two or four times.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="side-effects">Side Effects<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#side-effects" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Side effects include dry mouth, nausea, constipation, urinary retention, blurred vision, disorientation and confusion.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="electroconvulsive-therapy-ect">Electroconvulsive Therapy (ECT)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#electroconvulsive-therapy-ect" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Ugo Cerletti and Lucio Bini founded this method in 1938. It is given in doses ranging from 70 to 130 volts via electrodes placed on the temporal lobes from a machine constructed for treatment purposes.</p>
<p>Before ECT is administered, the following investigations are done:</p>
<ul>
<li>Physical examination like x-ray of the chest and spine</li>
<li>Electrocardiogram (ECG) and electroencephalogram (EEG) may be done</li>
</ul>
<p>At the same time, informed consent is obtained from the relatives after explaining the procedure. The night before ECT the patient is starved for six hours. Before taking the patient to the ECT department, all metallic objects are removed from the patient. Thereafter, premedication of atropine 0.6mg is given to dry body secretions. The patient is put under general anaesthesia, and then the doctor passes the current as explained earlier. The patient is secured on a theatre couch to prevent accidental fall.</p>
<p>The patient is then taken to the recovery room where vital signs are taken until the patient is fully awake. After that, the patient is given something to eat. In the ward, the patient should be closely observed, and later assessed to monitor the effect of ECT.</p>
<p>Treatments can be repeated if the patient does not improve. The frequency of treatment depends upon the severity of the patient's mental disorder. He may have two or three ECT treatments per week for a maximum of 8 to 12 treatments.</p>
<p>Nurses are responsible for setting up treatment and for the safety of the patient. Although deaths during treatments are rare, a supply of colamine to counteract barbiturates and the usual supply of emergency equipment must be at hand.</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 19 of 185
Bishop's Computers</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="psychological-treatments">Psychological Treatments<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#psychological-treatments" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Having completed your look at the physical treatment methods, you will now look at some of the psychological treatments used to treat patients suffering from mental health illness.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="psychotherapy">Psychotherapy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#psychotherapy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This is a form of treatment involving communication between the patient and the therapist, with the aim of modifying and alleviating illness.</p>
<p>A professional relationship is established, with the patient aimed at removing, modifying or mitigating the existing symptoms or disturbance patterns of behaviour or promotion of positive personality, growth and development.</p>
<p>There are two main types of psychotherapy:</p>
<ul>
<li>Individual psychotherapy</li>
<li>Group psychotherapy</li>
</ul>
<p>Individual Psychotherapy</p>
<p>Individual psychotherapy can be further subdivided into several categories.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="supportive">Supportive<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#supportive" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This deals with current problems and helps the patient to overcome their symptoms and cope with them satisfactorily in future.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="suggestive">Suggestive<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#suggestive" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This is a therapeutic method based on the belief that the patient has the ability to modify their abnormal emotional behaviour by applying their willpower and common sense.</p>
<p>Appeals are made to the patient's reason and intelligence. This is to help them abandon neurotic aims and symptoms and enable them to regain self respect.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="persuasive">Persuasive<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#persuasive" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This is the oldest form of psychotherapy. It is also widely used in advertising, propaganda, religious and political activities.</p>
<p>It revolves around a state of artificially induced suggestibility known as hypnosis. The technique is aimed at narrowing the patient's attention to the hypnotist alone.</p>
<p>Hypnosis ranges from a light hypnotic state to a deep trance. The main purpose of hypnosis is psychological investigation.</p>
<p>This deals with current problems and helps the patient to overcome their symptoms and cope with them satisfactorily in future.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="group-psychotherapy">Group Psychotherapy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#group-psychotherapy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The treatment of the patient by psychotherapy in groups was first introduced as a time saving measure, but subsequent experience demonstrated that, the method had special therapeutic value, which did not occur in individual psychotherapy.</p>
<p>There are various styles of group therapy. One example of a group therapy setting, might involve a group size of six to eight patients. The therapy would have a time span of 1 to 1.5 hours and sessions would be held once or twice weekly. A relaxed, informal style might be adopted, with the patients sitting in a circle to denote equality.</p>
<p>There are several benefits associated with the group therapy method. These include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Re-education of the patient with a view towards altering attitudes and behaviour patterns</li>
<li>Socialisation</li>
<li>Improved adjustment and adaptation to reality</li>
<li>Increased understanding of emotional problems and conflicts</li>
<li>Modification of personality and character</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="behaviour-therapy">Behaviour Therapy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#behaviour-therapy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This is defined as a therapeutic technique, which attempts to change the patient's behaviour directly rather than correct the basic cause of the undesirable behaviour.</p>
<p>The two main methods that are used are:</p>
<ol>
<li>Changing the behaviour from inside using covert and cognitive therapies. Here, the priority is to help the patient modify their view of the world and themselves, by helping them change the things they say about themselves.</li>
<li>Changing the behaviour from outside. This is achieved through positive reinforcement of acceptable behaviour and negative reinforcement for unacceptable behaviour.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="activity-therapy">Activity Therapy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#activity-therapy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>There are several forms of activity therapy.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="occupational-therapy">Occupational Therapy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#occupational-therapy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This involves the use of selected activities to improve general performance, to enable the</p>
<p>patient to learn the essential skills of day-to-day living and to assist in the reduction of symptoms. Activities may include painting, washing clothes and so on.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="recreation-therapy">Recreation Therapy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#recreation-therapy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This method uses activities like sports, games, hobbies to treat behaviour.</p>
<p>It lays the emphasis on re-socialisation, reality orientation and involvement of mentally ill persons.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="dance-therapy">Dance Therapy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#dance-therapy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It uses body rhythmic movements and interaction to express emotions, thereby increasing awareness of the body and ego strength.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="rehabilitation">Rehabilitation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#rehabilitation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is the process of restoring a person's ability to live and work as normally as possible after disabling injury or illness.</p>
<p>It is aimed at helping the patient achieve maximum possible physical and psychological fitness and regain the ability to care for themselves.</p>
<p>This aim is achieved through:</p>
<ul>
<li>Physical therapy</li>
<li>Occupational therapy</li>
<li>Vocational training</li>
<li>Industrial/ work therapy</li>
<li>Recreation or social therapy</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="section-4-management-of-commonmental-health-conditions">SECTION 4: MANAGEMENT OF COMMONMENTAL HEALTH CONDITIONS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#section-4-management-of-commonmental-health-conditions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="introduction">Introduction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>In this section you will be required to reflect on the classification of mental illness. This knowledge will assist you to better understand any of the conditions that might come under discussion. For each condition, efforts will be made to include definition, causes, psychopathology, clinical features, methods of diagnosis and management.</p>
<p>To avoid repetition, the content of psychopathology will be treated as a separate topic at the beginning. You will then be expected to apply the knowledge in all relevant mental health conditions</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="objectives">Objectives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>By the end of this section you will be able to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Define psychopathology</li>
<li>Describe mental illness</li>
<li>Describe some of the more frequent psychotic conditions</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="psychopathology">Psychopathology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#psychopathology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Psychopathology is defined as the study of abnormal states of mind. There are many approaches to psychopathology but in this material, developmental psychopathology will be used. This approach examines different maladaptive behaviours displayed during childhood, adolescence and adulthood. Since personality development is a continuous process, behaviour in childhood and adolescence do overlap. It is important to note that emotional problems in childhood can surface later and plague a person in adulthood.</p>
<p><strong>There are several vulnerability issues regarding children that you should always keep in mind.</strong></p>
<p>Since children do not have realistic view of themselves and their world, they have less self-understanding and have not developed a stable sense of identity. Therefore, children have less developed coping mechanisms when it comes to dealing with stressful situations. Children tend to use unrealistic concepts to explain events since they have limited perspectives. For example, in an effort to join a dead parent, the child may commit suicide.</p>
<p>Children are protected against stress by parents since they are dependent on them. However, if</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>the parents ignore the child, they experience rejection, disappointment and failure. Since children lack experience in dealing with problems, ordinary hardships are magnified.</p>
<p>Problems that look minor to adults easily hurt children causing psychological trauma. These series of traumatic experiences may surface later in life in the form of mental illness.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="schizophrenia">Schizophrenia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#schizophrenia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Schizophrenia is a group of mental disorders that presents with varied symptoms of disordered thinking and bizarre social behaviour. It affects approximately 1% of the total population, including adolescents and young adults. There is increased incidence in the lower social class. Patients with this condition occupy 50% of beds in mental hospitals.</p>
<p>Generally:</p>
<ul>
<li>25% of patients diagnosed with schizophrenia recover completely.</li>
<li>50 to 65% have residual symptoms and relapses.</li>
<li>Approximately 10% remain ill.</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260117-840536f7.jpeg" alt="img-1.jpeg"></p>
<p>There are several risk factors associated with the conditions. Schizophrenia is often witnessed in individuals with family members who have schizophrenia or in children who are:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Highly individualistic in their thought processes.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Overtly independent and obedient.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Shy, withdrawn and loners.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Unmanageable, prone to destructive, aggressive behaviour.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Truant from school.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Sensitive to separation.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>There is no single cause but research studies indicate several possible factors. These include possible hereditary factors or disturbances in the neurotransmitter system. The condition can also be traced back to disturbed family interaction patterns, for example, family schism and faulty familial communication and environmental stresses such as major crisis or migration.</p>
<p>The condition manifests in several ways. Early signs include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Blocking or cutting off conversation with friends</li>
<li>Expressing various body symptoms</li>
<li>Forgetting or abandoning plans or life goals</li>
<li>Disregarding social customs</li>
</ul>
<p>As the condition progresses, the patient exhibits a tendency towards separation, rejection or substance abuse like alcohol.</p>
<p>In the acute phase, the patient will experience:</p>
<ul>
<li>Auditory and visual hallucinations.</li>
<li>Illusions.</li>
<li>Delusions of persecution, grandeur or impending distraction.</li>
<li>Autistic thinking characterised by being highly personal.</li>
<li>Speech characterised by incoherence, echolalia, neologisms and unwillingness to speak.</li>
<li>Inappropriate behaviour, for example, grimacing, negativism, suggestibility and poor personal hygiene.</li>
<li>Blunting ambivalence and inappropriateness of affect.</li>
</ul>
<p>The next phase is known as the residual phase. At this stage, the patient usually exhibits symptoms of flat or blunt affect, rambling speech, poor hygiene and grooming and distortion of some perceptual experiences may persist.</p>
<p>Finally, in the chronic/relapse phase, the patient may point to feelings of boredom and apathy, impulsive suppression of feelings and psychotic disorganisation with increasing perceptual and cognitive dysfunction, loss of identity and loss of self-control.</p>
<p>There are several types of schizophrenia, which you will know look at in detail.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="catatonic-schizophrenia">Catatonic Schizophrenia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#catatonic-schizophrenia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is a disorder characterised by a stuporous state in which the person is mute, negative or complains in response to a request. The</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>individual may be immobile, display waxy flexibility and may retain urine and faeces.</p>
<p>It may alternatively be characterised by a highly excited state in which the person is abusive, aggressive, hyperactive or agitated (catatonic excitement).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="disorganised-schizophrenia">Disorganised Schizophrenia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#disorganised-schizophrenia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is a disorder characterised by incoherence, foolishness and regressive behaviour.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="paranoid-schizophrenia">Paranoid Schizophrenia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#paranoid-schizophrenia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is a disorder characterised by delusions of persecution or grandeur.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="undifferentiated-schizophrenia">Undifferentiated Schizophrenia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#undifferentiated-schizophrenia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This disorder is characterised by a variety of symptoms found in several of the types of schizophrenia that have previously been covered above, and are known as simple types.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="treatment">Treatment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The nurse should arrange short-term, intermediate and long-term goals for the patient on drug treatment</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="short-term-goals">Short-term Goals<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#short-term-goals" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>These are goals that can be accomplished in the shortest time interval and must be done before the patient can move on to accomplish other types of goals. For example, to ensure that the patient establishes contact with the nurse.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="intermediate-goals">Intermediate Goals<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#intermediate-goals" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>An intermediate goal might be for a patient to express their feelings in whatever mode they are able. This is not possible before the patient learns sufficient trust to share their painful and unacceptable thoughts. The patient must give up behaviours that hinder nurse-patient interaction in the working phase.</p>
<p>This goal involves certain behaviour on the part of the nurse that permits the patient to draw closer to them, including actual physical care of the patient.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="long-term-goals">Long-term Goals<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#long-term-goals" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>To attain this objective, the patient needs to trust other people, and to communicate fully enough so that others become familiar with the patient's symbolic representations and characteristic modes of thought.</p>
<p>Another long-term goal would be to help the patient identify living situations that cause them great anxiety and help them to learn how to</p>
<p>reduce their own tension before their ego begins to shatter under the impact of the forces impinging on them.</p>
<p>A variety of therapies are available and include the following:</p>
<ul>
<li>Short hospitalisation to assist with the problem of being a danger to themselves or others, of deviant behaviour that is abrasive to the family and community and monitoring effects of drugs or other therapies.</li>
<li>Outpatient treatment to provide aftercare, maintenance therapy, social support programs and medical clinics.</li>
<li>Rehabilitation services to provide opportunities to increase skills in living such as vocational rehabilitation, foster home care and halfway houses.</li>
<li>Drug therapy with antipsychotics to assist in alleviating symptoms and increasing patients availability for psychotherapy (refer to the section three on chemotherapy in treatments used in psychotherapy).</li>
<li>Individual and group psychotherapy to assist patient in daily problems by exploring relationships, sources of anxiety and coping techniques. In group therapy support is offered on how to cope with problems encountered in everyday life.</li>
<li>Family therapy to assist in defining the problem as one concerning the entire family rather than concerning the patient alone, to improve communication, to clarify roles within the family, to manage stress and to assist in problem solving.</li>
</ul>
<p>It is also important to provide some basic health education to the patient. This would include the following steps:</p>
<ul>
<li>Teach patient and family various ways of obtaining help in improving work, educational and social skills.</li>
<li>Stress the need for re-hospitalisation if the need arises.</li>
<li>Teach the patient how to take medication and how to tolerate and/or adapt to side effects of the drugs.</li>
<li>Patient and relatives should be taught how to identify stress early and then use problem solving skills.</li>
<li>Family members should be taught how to supervise the patient's medication and how to respond to disturbing behaviour.</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<ul>
<li>Provide information on the nature of schizophrenia and the treatments available.</li>
<li>Stress the importance of not using illicit drugs and alcohol.</li>
</ul>
<p>Nursing diagnosis of schizophrenia should refer to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Poor or lack of insight.</li>
<li>Non-compliance.</li>
<li>Aggression.</li>
<li>Impaired communication.</li>
<li>Suspiciousness.</li>
<li>Impulsiveness.</li>
<li>Sensory/perceptual alteration: visual, auditory, gustatory, kinaesthetic, tactile.</li>
<li>Self-care deficit: feeding/hygiene, dressing/grooming, toileting.</li>
<li>Coping is ineffective.</li>
<li>Suicidal tendencies.</li>
<li>Alteration of thought process.</li>
<li>Disturbance in self-concept, that is, disturbance in self-esteem, role performance and personal identity.</li>
</ul>
<p>For an individual to be diagnosed as having schizophrenia, symptoms must persist for six months with one month of acute symptoms.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="affective-disorders">Affective Disorders<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#affective-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Affective disorders are a group of mental disorders that present mainly with symptoms of mood disturbance with associated changes in thinking and behaviour. In terms of their incidence, females outnumber males 2:1. An estimated 20%-50% of people over 65 years of age experience depression.</p>
<p>Bipolar disorders occur before the age of 30, while depression occurs at any age. Depression occurring for the first time after the age of 40 frequently indicates underlying physical illness. Depression is frequently associated with other medical disorders or treatment, for example, alcoholism, cancer and/or the side effects of some drugs used in the treatment of hypertension.</p>
<p>No single causal factor has been identified but hypotheses and research indicate several possible causes. These include:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Genetic factors.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Disturbance in the neurotransmitters system, involving norepinephrine, serotonin, dopamine, acetylcholine.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Disturbance of steroid hormones.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Stressful life events prior to onset of illness.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Lack of social support.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Depression is hostility turned against yourself, while mania is hostility projected at others.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The individuals view themselves, the future and the current experiences in a negative way.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Family interaction patterns in which a child experiences high expectations of achievement by parents and little approval for being themselves.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>The conditions manifest in different ways depending on the type of disorder.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="major-depression">Major Depression<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#major-depression" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Symptoms include sadness, apathy, feelings of worthlessness, self-blame, thoughts of suicide, desire to escape, avoidance of simple problems, anorexia, weight loss, lessened interest in sex, sleeplessness, reduction in activity or ceaseless activity. In infants and older children, symptoms include a refusal to eat, listlessness, lack of activity, fear of death of a parent and fear of separation from parents. In adolescents, symptoms are social isolation, negative attitude, sulkiness, feeling of being unappreciated and acting out in antisocial ways.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="bipolar-disorder">Bipolar Disorder<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#bipolar-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is a disorder in which there are alternating periods of depression and mania. Bipolar disorder manic episodes exhibit symptoms of hyperactivity, speech pressure, hyper sexuality, delusions, abusive and sleeplessness. Meanwhile, bipolar disorder depressive episodes exhibit symptoms similar to those of major depression.</p>
<p>There are several forms of treatment. You will now look at some of these in more detail.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="hospitalisation">Hospitalisation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hospitalisation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is used in acute mania and in depression when there is evidence of poor judgment, weight loss and a lack of emotional support.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="drug-therapy-with-antidepressants-or-antimanic-drugs">Drug Therapy with Antidepressants or Antimanic Drugs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#drug-therapy-with-antidepressants-or-antimanic-drugs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Examples of drug therapy treatments include antidepressants. As a hypothetical treatment, using tricyclic medication, for example, imipramine. Build up to the effective dose over 7-10 days. Start with 25-50mg each night and build up to 100-150mg. Withdraw the medication</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers
Page 23 of 185</p>
<p>slowly and monitor for withdrawal reaction and to ensure remission is stable.</p>
<p>You can also use antimanic drugs.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="drug-therapy-with-antidepressants-or-antimanic-drugs">Drug Therapy with Antidepressants or Antimanic Drugs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#drug-therapy-with-antidepressants-or-antimanic-drugs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>If the patient displays excitement or disruptive behaviour, antipsychotic medication is needed initially, for example, haloperidol, at a dose of 1.5-4mg up to three times a day. In acute agitation, benzodiazepines may be used in the short term in conjunction with antipsychotic drugs, for example, diazepam 5-10mg up to four times a day.</p>
<p>Another drug that can be used is lithium. One usually commences or stops taking lithium with the advice of a specialist to help relieve mania and depression. It also prevents episodes from recurring. Levels of lithium in the blood must be measured frequently when adjusting the dose, and every three months in stable patients. Ten to fourteen hours post-dose the desired level is 0.4-0.8mmol/litre. Lithium should be stopped immediately if blood levels are more than 1.5mmol/litre or there is diarrhoea and vomiting.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="drug-therapy-with-antidepressants-or-antimanic-drugs">Drug Therapy with Antidepressants or Antimanic Drugs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#drug-therapy-with-antidepressants-or-antimanic-drugs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Other forms of treatment include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Electro Convulsive Therapy (ECT): used in severe depression or mania.</li>
<li>Psychotherapy used to deal with issues of dependency and manipulation of loss experience and self-destructiveness.</li>
<li>Behaviour therapy, which focuses on rewarding acceptable behaviour and providing social skills.</li>
<li>Maintenance of social support by family members, workmates, etc.</li>
<li>Assessment for suicide ideation particularly for the depressed patients and prompt intervention.</li>
<li>Health education is necessary to provide the patient with information about affective disorders, major treatments and prognosis.</li>
<li>Assist the patient and family in learning ways to manage stress.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="substance-use-disorders">Substance Use Disorders<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#substance-use-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Substance use disorders are a group of mental disorders manifested by impairments in social and occupational functions, which are related to</p>
<p>a regular use of specific substances that are intended to alter mood or behaviour.</p>
<p>Alcohol is one of the commonly used psychoactive substance. Alcoholism affects 7.5-10 million people worldwide, mainly those in early and middle adulthood. Substance abuse is more common in men than in women.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="presenting-complaints">Presenting Complaints<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#presenting-complaints" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Patients may be depressed, nervous or exhibit signs of insomnia. They may directly request a prescription for narcotics or other drugs, request help to withdraw, or help in stabilising their drug use.</p>
<p>They may present in a state of intoxication, withdrawal or physical complications of drug use, for example, abscess or thrombosis. They may also present with social or legal consequences of their drug use, for example, debt or prosecution. Occasionally, covert drug use may manifest itself as bizarre, unexplained behaviour.</p>
<p>Signs of drug withdrawal include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Opioids lead to nausea, sweating, hallucinations.</li>
<li>Sedatives lead to anxiety, tremors, hallucinations.</li>
<li>Stimulants lead to depression, moodiness.</li>
</ul>
<p>The family may request help before the patient does, as often, the patient is irritable at home, or missing work. The aim is to assist the patient to remain healthy until, if motivated to do so, and with the necessary help and support, they can achieve a drug-free life.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="diagnostic-features">Diagnostic Features<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnostic-features" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>There are several diagnostic features associated with substance abuse. These include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Physical harm, for example, symptoms of mental disorder due to drug use or a harmful social life leading to loss of a job, severe family problems or criminality.</li>
<li>Habitual or harmful drug use.</li>
<li>Difficulty in controlling drug use.</li>
<li>High tolerance, for example, the individual can use large amounts of drugs without appearing intoxicated.</li>
<li>Withdrawal, for example, anxiety, tremors or other withdrawal symptoms after stopping use.</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>The diagnosis will be aided by:</p>
<ul>
<li>Taking the patient's personal history (especially drug use).</li>
<li>Examination for needle tracts, complications, for example, thrombosis or viral illness.</li>
<li>Investigations for haemoglobin, Liver Function Tests (LFTs), urine drug screen and hepatitis B and C.</li>
</ul>
<p>Management</p>
<p>If the patient is not willing to stop or change drug use:</p>
<ul>
<li>Do not reject or blame the patient.</li>
<li>Advise the patient on harm-reduction strategies, for example, on the dangers of needle sharing by intravenous drug users.</li>
<li>Point out clearly the medical, psychological and social problems associated with drug use.</li>
<li>Make a future appointment to reassess health and discuss drug use.</li>
</ul>
<p>If the patient is willing to reduce the drug uses but not to quit completely:</p>
<ul>
<li>Negotiate a clear goal for decreased use, for example, not more than one marijuana or cigarette per day.</li>
<li>Discuss strategies to avoid or cope with high-risk situations.</li>
<li>Introduce self-monitoring procedures, for example, a diary of drug use.</li>
<li>Consider options for counselling and/or rehabilitation.</li>
</ul>
<p>If the patient opts to have a substitute drug:</p>
<ul>
<li>Negotiate a clear use of the prescribed substitute drug.</li>
<li>Discuss ways of avoiding high risk situations, for example social situations or stressful events.</li>
